</div>
			<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">List of Nobel laureates by university affiliation</h1>
									<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
									<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
								<div id="contentSub"></div>
												<div id="jump-to-nav" class="mw-jump">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
				</div>
				<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><p>This <b>list of Nobel laureates by university affiliation</b> shows the <a href="/wiki/University" title="University">university</a> affiliations of individual winners of the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel Prize</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Memorial_Prize_in_Economic_Sciences" title="Nobel Memorial Prize in Economic Sciences">Nobel Memorial Prize in Economic Sciences</a> since 1901 (total 892 individual laureates).<sup id="cite_ref-:8_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:8-1">[1]</a></sup> This list does not include organizations which were awarded the Nobel prize (as of 2017, 24 such organizations<sup id="cite_ref-:8_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:8-1">[1]</a></sup>) or any individuals affiliated with those organizations. However, an individual laureate who received the Nobel prize while working at a research organization formally affiliated with or operated by a university is counted as an affiliate of that university. Universities are listed in descending order according to the number of affiliates, while <b>only the top 50 universities are shown explicitly with their rankings.</b></p>
<p>The university affiliations in this list are all formal/official academic affiliations (i.e., official employment or degree program), which fall into three categories: 1) <i>Graduate and Attendee</i>, 2) <i>Long-term Academic Staff</i>, and 3) <i>Temporary Academic Staff</i>. Graduates are defined as those who hold Bachelor's, Master's, PhD, or equivalent degrees from a university, while attendees are those who formally enrolled in a degree-program at a university for at least one day but did not complete the program or obtain a degree (thus, honorary degrees, summer attendees, exchange students, and auditors are generally excluded). The category of "Long-term Academic Staff" mostly consists of tenure/tenure-track and equivalent academic positions, while that of "Temporary Academic Staff" mostly consists of lecturers (without tenure), postdoctoral researchers, visiting professors/scholars, and equivalent academic positions.</p>
<p>Further explanations on "Temporary Academic Staff" are presented as follows. Some visiting professorships/lectureships such as the "Morris Loeb Lecturer", "Lee Historical Lecturer" and "Charles Eliot Norton Professor" in <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard University</a> are in fact awards/honors/recognition instead of an actual affiliation with the university (compared to the "Morris Loeb Long-term Lecturer"),<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> and thus will not be counted in this list. In particular, giving lectures or doing researches at a university is not an indication of affiliation with that university&#160;– the lecturer/researcher has to be officially employed (even with a "visiting" title) by the university to be counted. Finally, summer employees and visitors are generally excluded from the list, and non-academic positions (e.g., advisory committee, administrative staff, etc) are also excluded.</p>
<p>In this list, the number following a person's name is the year he/she received the prize; in particular, a number with asterisk (*) means the person received the award while he/she was working at the institution containing that asterisk. A laureate with his/her name underlined implies that this person has already been counted for a same institution in some previous category. If a person had multiple positions under one category, only the position with highest rank is considered.</p>
<p>Each institution practices different methods for counting affiliates, from generous counting to conservative.<sup id="cite_ref-latimes2000-10-19_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latimes2000-10-19-4">[4]</a></sup> Within this list, the University Counts are thus shown as comparison, which are published by the universities themselves. The federal <a href="/wiki/University_of_London" title="University of London">University of London</a> is counted by its individual constituent colleges in this table. The <a href="/wiki/University_of_California" title="University of California">University of California</a> is also counted here by its individual campuses. Finally, this list, together with <b><a href="/wiki/List_of_Fields_Medal_winners_by_university_affiliation" title="List of Fields Medal winners by university affiliation">List of Fields Medal winners by university affiliation</a></b> and <b><a href="/wiki/List_of_Turing_Award_laureates_by_university_affiliation" title="List of Turing Award laureates by university affiliation">List of Turing Award laureates by university affiliation</a></b>, presents the university affiliation (with similar criteria) of people who have won highest honors in fundamental academic disciplines.</p>
<p>Legend: <abbr title="Physics" style="background:#b6ffb0">[Ph.]</abbr> Physics, <abbr title="Chemistry" style="background:#ffa0f0">[Ch.]</abbr> Chemistry, <abbr title="Physiology or Medicine" style="background:#ffb9a0">[PM]</abbr> Physiology or Medicine, <abbr title="Literature" style="background:#bdf6f8">[Li.]</abbr> Literature, <abbr title="Peace" style="background:#f5f18c">[Pe.]</abbr> Peace, <abbr title="Economics" style="background:#bdc4f8">[Ec.]</abbr> Economics.</p>
<p></p>

<td colspan="4"><a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard University</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> <span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States"><img alt="United States" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1235" data-file-height="650" /></a></span></td>

<td colspan="4"><b>Notes</b>: 1) Affiliates of <a href="/wiki/Radcliffe_College" title="Radcliffe College">Radcliffe College</a> ("Harvard Annex", 1879-1999) are not included in this list.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup>
<p>2) "Morris Loeb Lecturer" (short-term), "Lee Historical Lecturer" and "Charles Eliot Norton Professor" are not affiliates with Harvard University.</p>
<p>3) Harvard's University Count includes <a href="/wiki/Henry_Cadbury" title="Henry Cadbury">Henry Cadbury</a>, who represented the&#160;<a href="/wiki/American_Friends_Service_Committee" title="American Friends Service Committee">American Friends Service Committee</a> to receive the 1947 Nobel peace prize, and the Nobel-Peace-Prize (1985) winning <a href="/wiki/International_Physicians_for_the_Prevention_of_Nuclear_War" title="International Physicians for the Prevention of Nuclear War">International Physicians for the Prevention of Nuclear War</a>. They are both excluded from the following list.</p>

<td colspan="4"><a href="/wiki/Columbia_University" title="Columbia University">Columbia University</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> <span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States"><img alt="United States" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1235" data-file-height="650" /></a></span></td>

<tr>
<td colspan="4"><b>Notes</b>: 1) Affiliates of <a href="/wiki/Barnard_College" title="Barnard College">Barnard College</a> after 1900 (inclusive) are included in the following list.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[35]</a></sup>
<p>2) The "Ingeborg Rennert Professors" are not affiliates with Columbia University. For instance, <a href="/wiki/Elie_Wiesel" title="Elie Wiesel">Elie Wiesel</a> was an Ingeborg Rennert Professor of Judaic Studies at Barnard College, and is thus not included.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>3) The University Count of Columbia does not include attendees.</p>

<h2><span id="University_of_Chicago_(5th)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="University_of_Chicago_.285th.29">University of Chicago (5th)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Nobel_laureates_by_university_affiliation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: University of Chicago (5th)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Nobel_laureates_affiliated_with_the_University_of_Chicago" title="List of Nobel laureates affiliated with the University of Chicago">List of Nobel laureates affiliated with the University of Chicago</a></div>

<td colspan="4"><b>Notes:</b> 1) <a href="/wiki/Emily_Greene_Balch" title="Emily Greene Balch">Emily Greene Balch</a> and <a href="/wiki/T._S._Eliot" title="T. S. Eliot">T. S. Eliot</a> are included in the following list but not the University Count.
<p>2) Affiliates of <a href="/wiki/Argonne_National_Laboratory" title="Argonne National Laboratory">Argonne National Laboratory</a> (since 1946) and <a href="/wiki/Fermilab" title="Fermilab">Fermilab</a> (since 2007) are included in the list.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p>3) Affiliates of <a href="/wiki/Marine_Biological_Laboratory" title="Marine Biological Laboratory">Marine Biological Laboratory</a> starting 1 July 2013 are included in the list (e.g., <a href="/wiki/Eric_Betzig" title="Eric Betzig">Eric Betzig</a> was a lecturer from 1 to 10 May 2013, and is thus not included).<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[65]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[66]</a></sup></p>

<td colspan="4"><a href="/wiki/MIT" class="mw-redirect" title="MIT">Massachusetts Institute of Technology</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> <span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States"><img alt="United States" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1235" data-file-height="650" /></a></span></td>

<tr>
<td colspan="4"><b>Notes</b>: 1) MIT University Count includes <a href="/wiki/Susan_Solomon" title="Susan Solomon">Susan Solomon</a> and Wei-min Hao who were working in <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change" title="Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change">IPCC</a> which shared the 2007 Nobel Peace Prize as an organization, and <a href="/wiki/Eric_Chivian" title="Eric Chivian">Eric Chivian</a> who founded the IPPNW which was awarded the 1985 Nobel Peace Prize as an organization. These three people are thus excluded from this list.
<p>2) <a href="/wiki/Paul_Greengard" title="Paul Greengard">Paul Greengard</a> and <a href="/wiki/Richard_Thaler" title="Richard Thaler">Richard Thaler</a> are included in the following list but not the University Count.</p>

<p>2) Members of <a href="/wiki/G%C3%B6ttingen_Academy_of_Sciences_and_Humanities" title="Göttingen Academy of Sciences and Humanities">Göttingen Academy of Sciences and Humanities</a> are not included in the list, for the organization has no affiliation with the university. <sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[106]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Nobel_laureates_by_university_affiliation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-repeat2-14"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-repeat2_14-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-repeat2_14-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-repeat2_14-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-repeat2_14-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-repeat2_14-4"><sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-repeat2_14-5"><sup><i><b>f</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">This Nobel laureate received two Nobel Prizes. Counted only once because this is a list of laureates, not prizes.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-repeat-221"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-repeat_221-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-repeat_221-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-repeat_221-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-repeat_221-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-repeat_221-4"><sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-repeat_221-5"><sup><i><b>f</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-repeat_221-6"><sup><i><b>g</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-repeat_221-7"><sup><i><b>h</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-repeat_221-8"><sup><i><b>i</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">This Nobel laureate has more than one affiliation to this institution. </ol>

</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Nobel_laureates_by_university_affiliation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="refbegin" style="">
<p>The following list includes many university homepages listing Nobel Prize laureates affiliated to the respective university. Please note that the method of counting differs from university to university. Often, graduates are not included, and sometimes, researchers and faculty appointments after the award are not counted. Please consider that some of the pages are not up to date.</p>
</div>

[…] By 4pm, the Sharmas had had virtually the entire town of Vidisha visiting them. Almost every resident older than 50 has a story to tell about Kailash. Kailash had graduated in electrical engineering from the Samrat Ashok Technological Institute, Vidisha, and taught at a local polytechnic.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AList+of+Nobel+laureates+by+university+affiliation&amp;rft.atitle=A+street+rings+with+%E2%80%98Nobel%E2%80%99+cry&amp;rft.aufirst=Rasheed&amp;rft.aulast=Kidwai&amp;rft.date=2014-10-10&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Telegraph&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.telegraphindia.com%2F1141011%2Fjsp%2Fnation%2Fstory_18915372.jsp%23.VnMmkSCrQ8o&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span></li>
